## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of concentration (dA_dt) as a function of time (t) and concentration (A), which is the fundamental differential form of chemical reaction kinetics. The relationship typically follows rate laws dependent on reaction order, equilibrium constraints, or time-varying rate constants due to catalyst effects or changing conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate independent of concentration, typical for surface-saturated or photochemical reactions)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular decay or radioactive-like processes)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or collision-dominated processes)
- General power-law kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order for complex or diffusion-limited mechanisms)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (approach to chemical equilibrium in closed systems)
- Autocatalytic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-mediated acceleration with saturation, common in polymerization or chain reactions)
- Time-dependent rate decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or temperature ramp scenarios)
- Concentration-modulated time decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) * exp(c2 * A) (coupled temporal and concentration effects in aging or fouling systems)
- Dual-pathway parallel decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (simultaneous competing reaction mechanisms with different orders)
- Autoinhibition model: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (reaction rate suppression at high concentrations due to steric hindrance or crowding)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer/fractional reaction order → Log-log linearity: log(|dA_dt|) ≈ c1 * log(A) + c0 (slope directly indicates reaction order n)
- Equilibrium driving force → Linear concentration gap: dA_dt ≈ c0 * (c1 - A) (rate vanishes linearly as A approaches equilibrium value)
- Catalyst deactivation/aging → Time-modulated prefactor: dA_dt ≈ c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) or c0 * A * t**c1 (rate constant decays/increases monotonically with time)
- Autocatalytic feedback → Parabolic concentration dependence: dA_dt ≈ c0 * A * (c1 - A) (zero rate at initial and final states with a single peak)
- Parallel competing pathways → Additive multi-power law: dA_dt ≈ c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (distinct linear segments in log-log rate vs concentration plots)
- Diffusion/surface control → Fractional power scaling: dA_dt ≈ c0 * A**0.5 (transport-limited mechanisms yield non-integer exponents)
- Product inhibition/crowding → Exponential concentration suppression: dA_dt ≈ c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (super-polynomial decay of rate at high concentrations)

2. Linear in A times exponential in t: `k2 * A * exp(k3 * t)`

Let's check the candidates. They are mostly sums of terms. I need to find one that can represent exactly these three terms.

`A**2*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + c4 + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)`

Set `c0 = -0.5475`, `c1 = -0.5475`, `c2 = -0.03707`, `c3 = 0`, `c4 = 0`.
`c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)` -> `0.7049*cos(log(A+1))`
Set `c7 = 1`, `c6 = 1`, `c8 = pi/2`, `c5 = 0.7049`.
Matches exactly.

Candidate 3:
`A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2*(A + c3) + A*c4 + c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8 + 1) + c9)`
`A*c2*(A+c3) = c2*A**2 + c2*c3*A`.
Set `c2 = -0.5475`, `c3 = 0` -> `-0.5475*A**2`.
`A*c0*exp(c1*t)` -> `-0.5475*A*exp(-0.03707*t)`. Set `c0 = -0.5475`, `c1 = -0.03707`.
`A*c4 + c5` -> set `c4=0, c5=0`.
`c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8 + 1) + c9)` -> `0.7049*cos(log(A+1))`. Set `c8=1, c7=1, c9=pi/2, c6=0.7049`.
Matches exactly.

The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`-0.547523655303147*A**2 - 0.547523655303147*A*exp(-0.0370790480664167*t) + 0.704921991120659*cos(log(A + 1))`

It consists of three linearly independent basis functions:
1. Quadratic in `A`: `k1 * A**2`
2. Linear in `A` times exponential in `t`: `k2 * A * exp(k3 * t)`
3. Cosine of logarithm: `k4 * cos(log(A + 1))`

Using trigonometric identity `cos(x) = sin(x + π/2)`, the third term can be equivalently written as `k4 * sin(log(A + 1) + π/2)`. Any candidate must be able to represent these three exact functional forms. Extra polynomial or constant terms can be zeroed out by setting their free constants to 0.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK3)

GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A*exp(-c3*_s*t) + c4*_w*cos(log(A + c5))
Candidates evaluated: 68
Matched candidate IDs: [2, 3, 17]
Matched candidates: ["A**2*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + c4 + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8)", "A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2*(A + c3) + A*c4 + c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8 + 1) + c9)", "A*(A*c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)) + c3*sin(c4 + log(A + 1))"]

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.5475*A² - 0.5475*A*exp(-0.03708*t) + 0.7049*cos(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three terms:
1. A quadratic term: `c₀*A²`
2. An exponential decay term: `c₁*A*exp(c₂*t)`
3. A cosine of logarithm term: `c₃*cos(log(A + 1))`

Key basis functions: `A²`, `A*exp(αt)`, `cos(log(A+1))`

Let me analyze each candidate:

### Candidate 1: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2*(A+c3) + c4*sin(A*c5+c6) + c7*log(c8*exp(A*c9)+1)`
- Terms: `A*exp(t)`, `A²`, `A`, `sin(A)`, `log(exp(A)+1)` (softplus-like)
- Missing `cos(log(A+1))`. Has `sin(linear A)` and `log(exp(A)+1)` instead. These cannot combine to form `cos(log(A+1))`.
**Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: `A²*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + c4 + c5*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1) + c8)`
- Terms: `A²`, `A*exp(t)`, `A`, constant, `sin(c6*log(c7*A+1) + c8)`
- The last term: `sin(c6*log(c7*A+1) + c8)`. Setting c6=1, c7=1, c8=π/2 gives `sin(log(A+1) + π/2) = cos(log(A+1))`. ✓
- Extra terms `A*c3 + c4` can be zeroed by setting c3=0, c4=0.
**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 3: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2*(A+c3) + A*c4 + c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(A*c8+1) + c9)`
- Terms: `A*exp(t)`, `A²`, `A` (from c2*c3 and c4), constant, `sin(c7*log(c8*A+1)+c9)`
- Same as Candidate 2 essentially. Set c4=0, c5=0 (or absorb c3 into c4), and sin term → cos(log(A+1)).
**Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 4: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2*exp(A*c3) + c4*exp(A*c5) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8)`
- Has `A*exp(A*c3)` and `exp(A*c5)` — setting c3=0 gives `A*c2`, setting c5=0 gives `c4`. So we get `A*exp(t) + c2*A + c4 + c6*sin(A*c7+c8)`.
- Missing `A²` and `cos(log(A+1))`. `sin(linear A)` ≠ `cos(log(A+1))`.
**Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 5: Similar to 4 with extra `A*exp(A)` term. Same issues.
**Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 6: Has `(A+1)^5` — a 5th degree polynomial. Can't zero it without losing other terms. Also has `sin(A)` and `sin(log(A²+1))`. The `sin(c7*log(c8*A²+1)+c9)` — note it's A², not A+1. Even with c9=π/2, this gives `cos(log(c8*A²+1))` ≠ `cos(log(A+1))`.
**Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 7: `(c0 + (A*c1+c2)*(A*c3*exp(c4*t) + A*c5 + c5 + c6*sin(A*c7+c8)))/(A*c1+c2)`

- Has `1/(linear A)` term which can't be zeroed without making denominator infinite. Setting c0=0: `A*c3*exp(c4*t) + A*c5 + c5 + c6*sin(A*c7+c8)`. Missing `A²` and `cos(log(A+1))`.
**Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 8: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2*(A+c3) + c4*exp(A*c5) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8)`
- Setting c5=0: `c4` constant. Then: `A*exp(t) + A² + A + constant + sin(A)`. Missing `cos(log(A+1))`.
**Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 9: Simplifies to `A*c0/(A+c2) + c1*exp(c3*sin(A*c4+c5)) + A*c6*exp(c7*t) + A*c8 + c9`. Has `exp(sin(A))` — not equivalent.
**Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 10: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2*(A+c3) + c4*log(A*c5+1) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8)`
